    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText8957413367006074518" style="display:none">Six responsible adults. Three cute kids. One small dog. It’s just a normal weekend. What could possibly go wrong?<br /><br />Sam and Clementine have a wonderful, albeit, busy life: they have two little girls, Sam has just started a new dream job, and Clementine, a cellist, is busy preparing for the audition of a lifetime. If there’s anything they can count on, it’s each other.<br /><br />Clementine and Erika are each other’s oldest friends. A single look between them can convey an entire conversation. But theirs is a complicated relationship, so when Erika mentions a last minute invitation to a barbecue with her neighbors, Tiffany and Vid, Clementine and Sam don’t hesitate. Having Tiffany and Vid’s larger than life personalities there will be a welcome respite.<br /><br />Two months later, it won’t stop raining, and Clementine and Sam can’t stop asking themselves the question: What if we hadn’t gone?<br /><br />In Truly Madly Guilty, Liane Moriarty takes on the foundations of our lives: marriage, sex, parenthood, and friendship. She shows how guilt can expose the fault lines in the most seemingly strong relationships, how what we don’t say can be more powerful than what we do, and how sometimes it is the most innocent of moments that can do the greatest harm.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8957413367006074518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_29347945').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_29347945').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_29347945').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);

        });

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/933646-did-anyone-notice-that-the-true-the-only">Did anyone notice that the true, the only, hero of this book is the neighbor Harry? And Harry&#39;s backstory is heartbreaking. Why would not a single one of the six adult neighbors care enough to read a few newpapers, ask a few questions, to understand Harry, the ONLY character who seemed at all interested in the safety of the children? I think Harry is the key to the entire book. The bad guy is really the good guy.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I liked eventually learning about Harry's situation. However, even when we were learning about Harry's wife and son, he was still such an arsehole! Th<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I liked eventually learning about Harry's situation. However, even when we were learning about Harry's wife and son, he was still such an arsehole! The neighbors did try to get to know him, but he was...an arsehole! Rude to them all, even Dakota, except for Oliver whom he liked barely. Why would they even think to dredge up some obscure newspaper article on the tragedy, if it made the papers all?<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_1694742308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1694742308" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694742308?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694742308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10903370710043752023">Maybe I'm just spoiled by domestic thriller authors like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn' title='Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gillian Flynn</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29593.Megan_Abbott' title='Megan Abbott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Megan Abbott</a>, maybe I want all the wrong things from Moriarty, but whatever the reason, her books never pull me in. This is the third of her books that I've tried and once again I’m overcome by the <b>slowness</b>, the <b>lack of pull</b>… the sheer <b>dullness of the characters</b>.<br/><br/>Perhaps I do expect the wrong things, but I don't think that's completely my fault. I'm starting to realize that Moriarty's novels are given titles and descriptio</span>
  <span id="freeText10903370710043752023" style="display:none">Maybe I'm just spoiled by domestic thriller authors like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn" title="Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Flynn</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29593.Megan_Abbott" title="Megan Abbott" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Abbott</a>, maybe I want all the wrong things from Moriarty, but whatever the reason, her books never pull me in. This is the third of her books that I've tried and once again I’m overcome by the <b>slowness</b>, the <b>lack of pull</b>… the sheer <b>dullness of the characters</b>.<br /><br />Perhaps I do expect the wrong things, but I don't think that's completely my fault. I'm starting to realize that Moriarty's novels are given titles and descriptions that make them sound so much more dramatic and mysterious than they really are. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17802724.The_Husband_s_Secret" title="The Husband's Secret by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">The Husband's Secret</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19486412.Big_Little_Lies" title="Big Little Lies by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Little Lies</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty" title="Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Truly Madly Guilty</a> - secrets, lies and guilt, you say? Bring it on!<br /><br />Except her stories rarely venture outside of middle class soirées. The secrets are anticlimactic, leaving a "meh" sensation in their wake. I'm almost always left thinking “seriously, is that it?"<br /><br />I have to give credit where it's due - Moriarty seems in tune with human nature. She knows her characters well and they feel convincing. It was easy to imagine them as real people. <b>But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty" title="Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Truly Madly Guilty</a> lacks some grit; some drama</b>. <br /><br />It opens being deliberately coy about the events of a barbecue that took place several months previously. Clearly something important happened between Erika and Clementine's families, but the <b>snoozeworthy-pacing</b>, as the novel jumps between the day of the barbecue and the present, killed off most of my curiosity. Which, as it turned out, was just as well, because the answers are disappointing and the ending feels too neat.<br /><br />I'm sorry. I genuinely want to get on the Moriarty fanwagon, but I think it's time I admit her style is not one that draws me in, even if her titles and premises do. There are very few authors that can infuse everyday, mundane activities with tension (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29593.Megan_Abbott" title="Megan Abbott" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Abbott</a>, for one) but Liane Moriarty, for me, is not one of them. I feel like I’m reading a flier advertising dish soap.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10903370710043752023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1638726497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638726497" />
    <a title="Tanesha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1677632-tanesha"><img alt="Tanesha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226374314p2/1677632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638726497?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanesha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanesha" href="/user/show/1677632-tanesha">Tanesha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638726497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15325446658095460783">Oh geez, don't shoot the messenger here but this one left me flat. I'm a big fan of Liane Moriarty, but not only was this book about 200 pages too long, the storyline was weak, I didn't like any of the characters, and the "big reveal/secret" Moriarty usually puts in her books was a big letdown. Once it came out, and believe me, the almost 300 pages leading up to it was hard enough, all I could think was "that's what all of these people are going on about?" I think the main issue is that they jus</span>
  <span id="freeText15325446658095460783" style="display:none">Oh geez, don't shoot the messenger here but this one left me flat. I'm a big fan of Liane Moriarty, but not only was this book about 200 pages too long, the storyline was weak, I didn't like any of the characters, and the "big reveal/secret" Moriarty usually puts in her books was a big letdown. Once it came out, and believe me, the almost 300 pages leading up to it was hard enough, all I could think was "that's what all of these people are going on about?" I think the main issue is that they just aren't very likable or particularly interesting people. That's part of the point of many of her stories I know..bad things happen to normal people living in the burbs...but this group is more blah than usual. The rest is a back and forth between the characters that was still very slow to unfold and pretty predictable. Only my love for her past books got me to finish this - almost any other author, and I'd have stopped less than halfway through.<br /><br />I'll still read anything else Moriarty puts out, but this one sadly for me was not a good one at all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15325446658095460783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11569914326604957895">This <b>SLOW</b> building character-driven story of a disastrous BBQ truly tested my intestinal fortitude, but I stuck it out, and once I made it to the half-way point <i>(whew!)</i> when the <i>(ho hum)</i> proposal is <b>finally</b> made, the first shocking twist occurred tempting me to stay with it and discover what would happen next.<p><b>TRULY MADLY GUILTY</b> is a story that entices the reader in Chapter 1 to find out what <b>really</b> happened at an innocent neighborhood BBQ, but when Chapter 2 begins, a <b>SLOW</b> progression detailing </p></span>
  <span id="freeText11569914326604957895" style="display:none">This <b>SLOW</b> building character-driven story of a disastrous BBQ truly tested my intestinal fortitude, but I stuck it out, and once I made it to the half-way point <i>(whew!)</i> when the <i>(ho hum)</i> proposal is <b>finally</b> made, the first shocking twist occurred tempting me to stay with it and discover what would happen next.<p><b>TRULY MADLY GUILTY</b> is a story that entices the reader in Chapter 1 to find out what <b>really</b> happened at an innocent neighborhood BBQ, but when Chapter 2 begins, a <b>SLOW</b> progression detailing the inside scoop on three couples and their everyday, repetitive family lives left me feeling somewhat frustrated, <b>but.....</b> then the second heartbreaking twist occurs pulling me back in yet again convincing me I surely now had <b>all</b> the 'BBQ Day' answers; but nope, there was yet another <i>(somewhat predictable)</i> piece to the puzzle still to uncover.</p><p>Overall, an ok read, with ok characters, and an ok story with surprises, tense moments and even a bit of humor, but it does take a long time to get there.</p></span>

<div id="review_1567766109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567766109" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567766109?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567766109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14528643874206522214">Something terrible happened at a BBQ, a BBQ that three couples plus three young children attended. Whether this book works for the reader depends on patience, patience because it takes quite awhile before, we find out what happened. Not that a great deal, back stories of the characters, their thoughts, doesn't happen in alternating chapters, so it depends on how interesting you find their stories. Obviously it worked for me.<br/><br/>So much is happening here, a troubled marriage, a cellist with a big upc</span>
  <span id="freeText14528643874206522214" style="display:none">Something terrible happened at a BBQ, a BBQ that three couples plus three young children attended. Whether this book works for the reader depends on patience, patience because it takes quite awhile before, we find out what happened. Not that a great deal, back stories of the characters, their thoughts, doesn't happen in alternating chapters, so it depends on how interesting you find their stories. Obviously it worked for me.<br /><br />So much is happening here, a troubled marriage, a cellist with a big upcoming audition, IVF, hoarding, pole dancing, a resentful friendship etc. How this author puts this story together and makes it work is like a magic trick. So easy to read, flows right along, the two little girls providing a great deal of humor and the observations of people and marriages that can only be described as insightful. Easy to relate to because I know people like some of these in this book. The ending was a little pat for my taste but I so enjoyed getting there that I decided to leave my rating as it is. <br /><br />I haven't liked all her books as much as her last two but she has the knack of taking and exaggerating human foibles to put together amazing stories. Lighter fiction, because of the tone, but with a little bite. <br /><br />ARC from publisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14528643874206522214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1758830426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758830426" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467838647p2/22727329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1758830426?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781250069818" href="/book/show/26792235-truly-madly-guilty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758830426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16212878827335916341">Did you ever hear this old joke?<br/><br/><i>Worried that their son was too optimistic, the parents of a little boy took him to a psychiatrist. In an attempt to dampen the boy’s spirits, the psychiatrist showed him into a room piled high with nothing but horse manure. Instead of displaying disgust, the little boy climbed to the top of the pile and began digging.<br/><br/>“What are you doing?” the psychiatrist asked.<br/><br/>“With all this s**t” the little boy replied, beaming, “there must be a pony in here somewhere!”</i><br/><br/>That’s ho</span>
  <span id="freeText16212878827335916341" style="display:none">Did you ever hear this old joke?<br /><br /><i>Worried that their son was too optimistic, the parents of a little boy took him to a psychiatrist. In an attempt to dampen the boy’s spirits, the psychiatrist showed him into a room piled high with nothing but horse manure. Instead of displaying disgust, the little boy climbed to the top of the pile and began digging.<br /><br />“What are you doing?” the psychiatrist asked.<br /><br />“With all this s**t” the little boy replied, beaming, “there must be a pony in here somewhere!”</i><br /><br />That’s how I felt about reading this latest from Moriarty. I’m not comparing the book to a pile of manure, I’m just saying I ‘dug’ through a lot of pages and never found the pony. And I should point out I really, really like her books, I’ve read four out of the last six. I wouldn’t describe her books as literary, but for sheer entertainment and wickedly good fun Liane is my go to guilty pleasure, but this one was a long, torturous road to dullsville. I should have listened to the critics.<br /><br />Moriarty’s usual bag of tricks is on full display here, she serves up a steamer trunk worth of baggage from infertility to alcoholism to hoarding and beyond, but as opposed to her previous books, it is lacking in humor and the characters are just not that interesting. The most exasperating factor for me, however, was the foreshadowing that felt artificial and forced for the first 200+ pages. By the time I reached the pivotal reveal my irritation had multiplied, yet I slogged on because surely NOW we would get to the Moriarty formula I’ve come to love, but it was not to be. No pony for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16212878827335916341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1598150993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1598150993" />
    <a title="Jessica Jeffers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/188447-jessica-jeffers"><img alt="Jessica Jeffers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459125628p2/188447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1598150993?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Jeffers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Jeffers" href="/user/show/188447-jessica-jeffers">Jessica Jeffers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/188447-jessica-jeffers?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1598150993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16280217045847172856">At one point, I was sure that I was going to give this two stars. And then I read a little farther and was certain that it had redeemed itself enough that I might give it four. I have so many mixed feelings about this book. Ultimately, I think I landed somewhere right in the middle of loving it and hating it. Three stars doesn't necessarily mean this is an average book; it just reflects my complicated feelings about it. <br/><br/>Because there’s some things that Liane Moriarty does extremely well here. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText16280217045847172856" style="display:none">At one point, I was sure that I was going to give this two stars. And then I read a little farther and was certain that it had redeemed itself enough that I might give it four. I have so many mixed feelings about this book. Ultimately, I think I landed somewhere right in the middle of loving it and hating it. Three stars doesn't necessarily mean this is an average book; it just reflects my complicated feelings about it. <br><br>Because there’s some things that Liane Moriarty does extremely well here. She paints amazingly complex portraits of realistic, flawed people. Their relationships to each other, the inner lives kept secret from even their spouses, the paths of their psychologies—all so well-drawn. These are characters that are so real that it’s almost uncomfortable to read about them. <br><br>She draws things out way too much, though. In doing so, Moriarty violates one of my biggest reading pet peeves (and this is totally subjective so it may not be a big deal to you): she builds suspense not by writing about suspenseful action or by showing us characters trying to solve a mystery but by simply withholding information from the reader. Which is a tactic that makes me kind of want to:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416046ra/821534.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The basic thrust of this story is that three couples get together for a barbecue and SOMETHING BAD happens at the barbecue that creates new fault lines in their relationships. We spend 250 pages reading characters saying to themselves and to each other, “If only I hadn’t gone to that barbecue” or “Nothing’s been the same since that barbecue.” She’d cut the alternating chapters off at odd points in an attempt to build in mini-cliffhangers, so you never knew what chapter would eventually reveal the big secret. Invariably, whatever happens at that barbecue is going to pale in comparison to the hand-wringing that’s led up to it. The actual event turns out to be a great hook to build a story around, but I was weirdly let down by its reveal because Moriarty’s storytelling style had led me to believe that it would be so much more salacious that it was. <br><br>And she uses this tactic on too many separate threads. Not only is there a big secret about the event at the barbecue, but each of the six adults have their own baggage that’s gotta be teased out to some extent. Why does Erika avoid dinner with her mother so much? Why is Tiffany so afraid of running into the guy from her daughter’s school? Why isn’t Sam talking to his wife about his new job? Yeah, this stuff helps develop the characters, but it also just adds extra pages to an already stuffed-full narrative. Some of these threads easily could have been spun off into their own novel and Moriarty would've had two much stronger novels instead of one that left me with so many mixed feelings. <br><br>And yet, as frustrated as I was, I enjoyed the book quite a bit. Moriarty's goal here seems to have been to examine how guilt drives us: feeling guilty about the decisions we've made that maybe didn't pan out the way we'd hoped, the weight of expectations and the fear that we might not live up to them, the regret we feel over actions we might not have even meant to take. She examines these ideas from many different facets and never seems to forget this goal, but, aside from the title, she doesn't pound you over the head with reminders that "Sam feels guilty." <br><br>Something else that Moriarty does exceptionally well here is shifting points of view. The chapters bounce back and forth between characters in the before-and-after of the barbecue, examining how each of the adults feel about the main plot twist and the psychodynamic reasons for their responses. She points out the different ways that characters feel about the same things as a way of demonstrating that we might not really know the people in our lives we claim to be closest to. It's interesting and it definitely helps develop her characters into such realistic people. But I did sometimes find myself wondering if any of them were ever at all even the least bit up-front and honest with each other. <br><br>I think that this could have been a four- or five-star read for me if Moriarty had just reined herself in a bit. Focus more on a single event instead of six characters' little secrets <i>and</i> a central event, and definitely cut down on the phony build-up. Her attempt to bring everything full circle at the end feels a bit forced, primarily just because she's given herself so much to wrap up, but she still manages to drop a few last-minute twists into the mix in a way that actually feels surprising. Even if you're feeling fatigued by all the "what-ifs" peppered in along the way, you'll be glad you hung in until the bitter end. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16280217045847172856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1683552121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1683552121" />
    <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf"><img alt="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540171256p2/9185509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1683552121?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf">Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf?shelf=aussie-authors">aussie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf?shelf=publisher-pan-macmillan">publisher-pan-macmillan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1683552121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18413028274385783000">Alright, before I begin my review of this book I need to admit something. A secret shame. This is my very first Liane Moriarty book! Yes I know, I know! I can hear you SHARPLY GASP! Her books seem right up my alley, how could I have not read Big Little Lies, or The Husband's Secret? "SHAME ON YOU MELISSA!" I hear you yell! "She is one of Australia's most loved authors!!" I have heard such good things, but guiltily have never had the chance or inclination to read them before. However, this means </span>
  <span id="freeText18413028274385783000" style="display:none">Alright, before I begin my review of this book I need to admit something. A secret shame. This is my very first Liane Moriarty book! Yes I know, I know! I can hear you SHARPLY GASP! Her books seem right up my alley, how could I have not read Big Little Lies, or The Husband's Secret? "SHAME ON YOU MELISSA!" I hear you yell! "She is one of Australia's most loved authors!!" I have heard such good things, but guiltily have never had the chance or inclination to read them before. However, this means that I came into reading Truly Madly Guilty with an unbiased perspective, and will hopefully give you a run down about what I liked and didn't like about it as a Moriarty novice!<br /><br />Something happened at the BBQ that day. Clementine didn't even want to go, and a major life-changing event occurred. Something that will change all of their lives. This is the story of three marriages, friendship, and the fateful events of one seemingly ordinary afternoon that will become extraordinary in their memories.<br /><br />Now, if you are after a light, feel good read then look elsewhere. This story is gritty, raw and deep.<br /><br />Moriarty creates an amazingly charged atmosphere in the first half of the book without actually revealing what happened at the BBQ! I found this SO FRUSTRATING! But not in a bad way! I was DESPERATE to know what happened. So desperate that when it did happen I felt slightly let down, as it went in a different direction than I was expecting. But I assume that's the point.<br /><br />I enjoyed the way it switched back and forth in time and from each different characters perspective. It was an extremely character driven novel which I can only assume is a Moriarty trademark by reading reviews of her other work. It was done masterfully. Each character was so inherently unique and imperfect. I was quickly sucked into their lives and relationships.<br /><br />It touched on SO MANY themes! Friendship, love, lust, family, parenting, childlessness, IVF, marriage, and mental illness just to name a few. However, with so much going on I found it dragged on a little bit for me. I was willing it at times to just get to the BBQ. However once it did get to the BBQ, I found the pace improved, even if it went in a direction I was not entirely anticipating. And there were a few excellent twists that I never saw coming, and that's always a big plus for me!<br /><br />Would I recommend Truly Madly Guilty?<br /><br />Absolutely worth the read! I will be definitely checking out her other books! I can't believe I have waited so long!<br /><br />Many thanks to Pan Macmillan Australia for an advanced copy of Truly Madly Guilty in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />For more reviews check out my <br /> <a href="http://www.booksbabiesbeing.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a><br /> <a href="http://www.facebook.com/booksbabiesbeing" rel="nofollow noopener">FACEBOOK</a><br /> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/BBB_Mel" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_1680189192" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680189192" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1680189192?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680189192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3571207912735980664">I enjoyed this very much but you do have to be patient! We all know something happens at the barbecue but the reader is not let into the secret until half way through the book which is a long time to wait! However the author gives us lots of back story to fill all those pages and I found myself intrigued. <br/><br/>The problem with such a build up is whether the event, when it materialises, will be as bad as we are expecting or will it be an anti climax. Fortunately Moriarty picks the kind of event which </span>
  <span id="freeText3571207912735980664" style="display:none">I enjoyed this very much but you do have to be patient! We all know something happens at the barbecue but the reader is not let into the secret until half way through the book which is a long time to wait! However the author gives us lots of back story to fill all those pages and I found myself intrigued. <br /><br />The problem with such a build up is whether the event, when it materialises, will be as bad as we are expecting or will it be an anti climax. Fortunately Moriarty picks the kind of event which terrifies us all and which totally lives up to expectations. I was also caught by surprise because everything indicates a very different scenario! The rest of the book is a study of three separate marriages and the intricacies of friendship. I found it all interesting and well worth reading.<br /><br />Maybe not quite as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19486412.Big_Little_Lies" title="Big Little Lies by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Little Lies</a> but it is close. I found it very readable and very hard to put down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3571207912735980664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2913599851?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2913599851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16066369836242185654">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars!! <br/><br/><br/>I really enjoy Liane Moriarty’s novels. “Big Little Lies” is one of my favorite books. I’ve had this audiobook for quite a while. I’m surprised it took me so long to get to it.<br/><br/><strong>
  <em>“Six responsible adults. Three cute kids. One small dog. It’s just a normal weekend. What could possibly go wrong?”</em>
</strong><br/><br/>This novel had a lot of characters but I thought they were all very well-developed. I especially loved the children, Ruby</span>
  <span id="freeText16066369836242185654" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />3.5 Stars!! <br /><br /><br />I really enjoy Liane Moriarty’s novels. “Big Little Lies” is one of my favorite books. I’ve had this audiobook for quite a while. I’m surprised it took me so long to get to it.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Six responsible adults. Three cute kids. One small dog. It’s just a normal weekend. What could possibly go wrong?”</em>
</strong><br /><br />This novel had a lot of characters but I thought they were all very well-developed. I especially loved the children, Ruby and Holly. They were sweet and funny, even when they were being naughty. I honestly did laugh out loud a few times.<br /><br />The story is told from multiple points of view. It did take a little while to get everyone straight, but once I figured out who was who, it was easy enough to follow along. It could possibly have been a little shorter as it did drag on at times.<br /><br />We hear from the characters in the present and back to the day of the barbeque. Right from the start, we are aware that something big happened at this barbecue.<br /><br />It was to be an ordinary neighborhood barbeque in an ordinary backyard with ordinary people.<br /><br />I really wanted to know what happened on that “<strong>
  <em>ordinary day</em>
</strong>”.<br /><br />I would never have guessed.<br /><br />The story deals with a lot of issues. I really liked how the author portrayed the relationships between husbands and wives, friends, parents, and children, etc. Most of the interactions felt very real and honest.<br /><br />This novel was a nice change of pace after some of the thrillers I’ve read lately. It wasn’t an intense read, although there were some emotional moments. The story kept me engaged.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a very interesting character-driven novel.<br /><br />I really liked the narrator, Caroline Lee. She’s narrated quite a few of Liane Moriarty’s novels.<br /><br />As usual, I’m excited to see what Liane Moriarty comes up with next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16066369836242185654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2029362196?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27831371-truly-madly-guilty">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2029362196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5965991977524788362">Obviously I loved this. I read it all in one day. Her books are so <b>addictive</b>—that's the best word to describe them. The epitome of a page turner.<br/><br/>Like I said in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1933703356?type=review#rating_121004600' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review of Big Little Lies</a>, Moriarty is great at crafting complex characters. The 6 adults, and even the 3 children, in this story or so well developed and interesting. They have flaws and personalities that will make you love them and hate them. It's that complexity that takes this book from 'soap opera'-esque to engaging and compellin</span>
  <span id="freeText5965991977524788362" style="display:none">Obviously I loved this. I read it all in one day. Her books are so <b>addictive</b>—that's the best word to describe them. The epitome of a page turner.<br /><br />Like I said in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1933703356?type=review#rating_121004600" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of Big Little Lies</a>, Moriarty is great at crafting complex characters. The 6 adults, and even the 3 children, in this story or so well developed and interesting. They have flaws and personalities that will make you love them and hate them. It's that complexity that takes this book from 'soap opera'-esque to engaging and compelling. She ups the ante by devoting the time to creating interesting humans at the center of an interesting story.<br /><br />Plus, her writing is <i>on point</i>. I love the little nuggets of wisdom she drops here and there. They stick out like little gems that you want to collect and treasure. Another reason this isn't your regular dollar store thriller.<br /><br />I can't wait to read everything else she's written. I have a feeling she's going to become one of my favorite authors and a go-to recommendation for people who don't know what to read next. You won't be able to put this down.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1641426778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641426778" />
    <a title="Andrew Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith"><img alt="Andrew Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605605555p2/5885760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1641426778?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Smith" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith">Andrew Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5885760-andrew-smith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641426778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15909020932610932940">What do people want from their lives? What is important to them and what trade-offs are they prepared to accept to achieve their goals? And how do we deal with the surprising and sometimes shocking situations life throws at us? These questions seem to me to be at the centre of Moriarty’s stories of modern day suburban life, set in and around Sydney, Australia. There’s normally quite a bit of humour, a cast of colourful characters and a sting or two in the tale. I thought her last book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19486412.Big_Little_Lies' title='Big Little Lies by Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'> Big Littl</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15909020932610932940" style="display:none">What do people want from their lives? What is important to them and what trade-offs are they prepared to accept to achieve their goals? And how do we deal with the surprising and sometimes shocking situations life throws at us? These questions seem to me to be at the centre of Moriarty’s stories of modern day suburban life, set in and around Sydney, Australia. There’s normally quite a bit of humour, a cast of colourful characters and a sting or two in the tale. I thought her last book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19486412.Big_Little_Lies" title="Big Little Lies by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener"> Big Little Lies</a> was sensational, her best yet – could she do it again with this one?<br /><br />There’s a set in stone format to the author’s story telling. The reader is advised that something has happened that has thrown lives into turmoil. This can be via a series of conversations we overhear or by other means but one thing is for sure, we won’t know the full truth about the ‘incident’ or the ‘secret’ until the last knockings. <br /><br />The cast this time around:<br /><br />- Clementine, husband Sam and children Holly (5) and Ruby (2). Sam’s moved up the career ladder to a new job in advertising and Clementine is a cellist, longing for the opportunity to be a permanent member of an established orchestra.<br /><br />- Erica and Oliver. Childless career types who are somewhat lacking in humour. God parents to Holly and Ruby. They both had challenging upbringings, courtesy of troubled parents.<br /><br />- Vid, his wife Tiffany and daughter Dakota. Vid is a larger than life party animal, Tiffany is sexy and alluring and with a colourful past. They are neighbours of Erica and Oliver.<br /><br />The scenario here is that the three couples and their children have recently attended a barbeque at Vid and Tiffany’s house. It’s caused a huge outfall and all three couples are ruminating over the ramifications and the potential damage to relationships and future plans. All sorts of emotions are on display. We initially pick up the period shortly after the event but as we move through the book these passages are interspersed with a fractured but detailed breakdown of the fateful day itself.<br /><br />There is less humour here than in some of the author’s books, but the individual stories of the three couples keep the interest alive and the dialogue is as sharp and true as ever. There are some genuine surprises stored up too, though the ending itself didn’t exactly provide a bombshell moment. In fact, the main events of the barbeque are declared quite early on and it’s the ramifications and side-stories that maintain the interest thereafter.<br /><br />It is an enjoyable tale and it does have some real depth to it. I read most of it perched on a beach bed in the Mediterranean and this helped establish, in my own mind at least, that it’s a pretty good holiday read. But this book doesn’t have the impact of her best work and I’m now wondering why Morriarty sticks so rigidly to her basic structure – maybe it’s time for a change as I think it’s getting to feel just a little tired.<br /><br />My thanks to Penguin UK and NetGalley for providing a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15909020932610932940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1830466473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830466473" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830466473?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830466473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1398789871978099981">Truly Madly Guilty is the telling of a BBQ event where things go wrong. The book focuses on 6 adults and 3 kids so that every aspect of a family can be brought to the table. The first half of the book is slow as molasses and sometimes I had to refrain myself from reading ahead and skimming to the juicy parts.<br/><br/>We get to know of the characters' past while the book is building up to this big reveal. To be honest I've already forgotten a lot about the early segments of the book. I thought the book wa</span>
  <span id="freeText1398789871978099981" style="display:none">Truly Madly Guilty is the telling of a BBQ event where things go wrong. The book focuses on 6 adults and 3 kids so that every aspect of a family can be brought to the table. The first half of the book is slow as molasses and sometimes I had to refrain myself from reading ahead and skimming to the juicy parts.<br /><br />We get to know of the characters' past while the book is building up to this big reveal. To be honest I've already forgotten a lot about the early segments of the book. I thought the book was so austere, strict in its format, and sometimes bland that I couldn't see myself give it 4 stars or write an interesting review (the bane of the review writer).<br /><br />I had read Big Little Lies recently and thought that I would enjoy this one just as much, but it was not to be. I can't put my finger on why it was so. The author displays her mercurial talent here, just as in Big Little Lies. But something was off about Truly Madly Guilty. Maybe the ordinary halves of the characters was shoved in our faces too much, I don't know. I give this book 3 stars, and do recommend it to fans of the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1398789871978099981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839265280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7430566135715163454">4 1/2 stars<br/><br/>This is one of those long, drawn-out stories that's more about character assessment and the hardships of life than it is a story based on its plot.<br/><br/>This is about 3 couples and how they react and cope with something that happens at a BBQ one afternoon. By the time Liane Moriarty unveils the secret, you'll be just over halfway done with the book.<br/><br/>I feel I should warn you though: Please don't expect the twist to be overly shocking, twisted or scandalous. I did have that expectation, merely</span>
  <span id="freeText7430566135715163454" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars<br /><br />This is one of those long, drawn-out stories that's more about character assessment and the hardships of life than it is a story based on its plot.<br /><br />This is about 3 couples and how they react and cope with something that happens at a BBQ one afternoon. By the time Liane Moriarty unveils the secret, you'll be just over halfway done with the book.<br /><br />I feel I should warn you though: Please don't expect the twist to be overly shocking, twisted or scandalous. I did have that expectation, merely because the topic was built up so much and was cleverly avoided. It kept me turning the page in anticipation, only to feel anti-climactic.<br /><br />That's ok, all is forgiven because the writing is superb. Liane Moriarty is quite skillful at weaving deep epiphanies, innermost feelings, etc. into her books, and yet you won't get confused or lost in the shuffle. She manages to do this while fluidly whipping back and forth from past to present. <br /><br />That requires great skill as a writer, and is something I personally admire, because it allows me to trust her blindly enough to sit back and soak in her story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7430566135715163454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1576876722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576876722" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576876722?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781427272874" href="/book/show/25991107-truly-madly-guilty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=goodreads-choice-award">goodreads-choice-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=womens-fiction-chicklit">womens-fiction-chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=stand-alone-novel">stand-alone-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576876722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14535837085137870401">★★★½<br/>If you have read any reviews for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty' title='Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'>Liane Moriarty</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty' title='Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'>Truly Madly Guilty</a>, you already know that it all seems to be about something that happened at a barbecue. Be forewarned, it's much too easy to get sucked into the mystery of what happened...afterall, the hush hush event is brought up over and over and over again and appears to be something horrendously taboo based on how the characters continue to refer to it. But I beg you, for your own enjoyment, ignore these traps. Instead, meet the charac</span>
  <span id="freeText14535837085137870401" style="display:none">★★★½<br />If you have read any reviews for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty" title="Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Liane Moriarty</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty" title="Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Truly Madly Guilty</a>, you already know that it all seems to be about something that happened at a barbecue. Be forewarned, it's much too easy to get sucked into the mystery of what happened...afterall, the hush hush event is brought up over and over and over again and appears to be something horrendously taboo based on how the characters continue to refer to it. But I beg you, for your own enjoyment, ignore these traps. Instead, meet the characters, learn about their relationships and most importantly, learn from them. <br /><br />Ms. Moriarty's strength is in her characters. I have written the following statement in every single review I've written for her: It's as if she has personally lived her characters' lives. The issues are real, the reactions are believable, and the emotions are palpable. In my opinion, her continued reminders of the mysterious barbecue incident were incredibly distracting and did a horrendous disservice to her story. Based on my own personal reading experience, the incident isn't shocking at all because once it's laid out for you, you'll realize it isn't anything you didn't already know about. Yes, there are some mild twists and one particular revelation saved for the end that gives a sad little jolt but the infamous barbecue incident does not warrant your focus. Focus on the characters, ignore the barbecue, and you'll be fine.<br /><br />Note: This book is long and it felt long, likely because the content dragged a bit. The first half is pretty slow. I listened via audio and although the narration was incredibly well-done, I was tempted to just skip to the end several times. I mean, it's 17 hours! But I hung in there and after all is said and done I don't regret it. Keep listening after the book is over because a few minutes at the very end features an interview between the audiobook narrator Caroline Lee and Ms. Moriarty. It wasn't a must-listen but it was a nice addition.<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“Everybody wants the babies...The cute little babies. But what they really need is foster parents for the older kids. The angry ones. The broken ones.”</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14535837085137870401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952977727?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LeAnne: GeezerMom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LeAnne: GeezerMom" href="/user/show/7862560-leanne-geezermom">LeAnne: GeezerMom</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952977727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2820701159605104238"><b>Shame on me. </b>I find myself rather shocked to have been so bowled over by a novel written by an author who I've pre-judged as a purveyor of chick-lit for the masses. I'm guilty of thinking myself too high brow, too science-y to succumb to the charms of a 'woman's writer'. Such a snob.<br/><br/>I was wrong. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty' title='Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'>Liane Moriarty</a> has got it going on, and I will read anything else she publishes from this point forward. For those female readers out there who also regard themselves as more selective than the average w</span>
  <span id="freeText2820701159605104238" style="display:none"><b>Shame on me. </b>I find myself rather shocked to have been so bowled over by a novel written by an author who I've pre-judged as a purveyor of chick-lit for the masses. I'm guilty of thinking myself too high brow, too science-y to succumb to the charms of a 'woman's writer'. Such a snob.<br /><br />I was wrong. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty" title="Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Liane Moriarty</a> has got it going on, and I will read anything else she publishes from this point forward. For those female readers out there who also regard themselves as more selective than the average woman, don't dismiss Moriarty like I did.<br /><br />The quick assessment? Six beautiful and deep character studies. Frequent dabs of humor. Relatable to anyone who has had a long term friendship since childhood. The destination is not the goal, but the journey is. If you cannot handle intentionally being made to wait, this will aggravate you. If you <i>can</i> handle the patent agreement with the author that she is not going to tie the bow and add the gift card until the very end, then this may thrill you. The audio version is outstanding!<br /><br />Background. The only - <b>and I mean ONLY</b> - reason her books are on my shelves is that two of them have been chosen by one of my book clubs (the one made up of only women). Just the very title of The Husband's Secret had me rolling my eyes, and while it was a little far fetched and too relationship-oriented for me to take seriously, I didn't hate it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19486412.Big_Little_Lies" title="Big Little Lies by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Little Lies</a>actually surprised me - it had a touch of that shallowness I had anticipated, but knowing that the big reveal about the murder mystery would not come until the end, I suspended my expectations and ended up really enjoying the book despite myself. My kids are still in school, so the mommy-wars aspect tickled me, and since I worked as a background actor in the movie BAD MOMS (along with my then-12 yr old son), it was even more fun - and yet had some very deep issues within it. She explored those serious topics exceptionally well.<br /><br />When the seven episode series for Big Little Lies came out on HBO, two of the gals from said book club invited me to meet with them over lunch every other week to binge-watch a couple of episodes each time. The series was incredibly well done - better than the book, even - and we ended up getting the husbands to watch the whole series and closed the season with a finale dinner-party (in costume). Awesome!<br /><br />I was intrigued with the backstory of how Reese Witherspoon and Nicole Kidman came to option BLL into this seven hour series and started reading up on how it came to be. A few of the various articles said that they had also optioned Truly Madly Guilty because the writing bowled them over.<br /><br />That was all I needed to read. Witherspoon and Kidman were right. THIS book? Wow.<br /><br />It is a character study, no doubt about it, so for those who need action to keep them interested, TMG may not work well. The book length is a bit hefty, but as in Big Little Lies, I knew that the various revelations would not come until the very end. I'm okay with that and in fact enjoy a drawn out lead up when the writing is great. And this is.<br /><br />There are six characters whose perspectives are played out in the story, and they pop around a bit in their timelines. As mentioned above, I listened to this via audio and found myself charmed by and drawn into every one of their interior voices. The peripheral characters - beyond the primary six - are drawn with depth and humor and feeling. <br /><br />Was I guilty of snotty prejudice towards Moriarty's writing? Truly. Am I also mad for her work? Guilty. Five stars and (incredibly!) on my Favorites Shelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2820701159605104238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6948101484985251602" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>I arrived late to the Liane Moriarty party, but after reading both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793553174?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">What Alice Forgot</a> and <a href="url" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Little Lies</a> this year I’ve been declaring to anyone who would listen . . . .<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489508458ra/22221825.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Moriarty took the art<s>ist</s>form formerly known as “Chick Lit” to a whole new level with likeable bitches as main characters and stories where skeletons fall out of pert near everyone’s closets. I put myself on the waiting list for <i>Truly Madly Guilty</i> at both libraries as soon as I finished my first Moriarty book, and I’m still 71st in line at the main branch if that is any indication on how popular this author has become. Unfortunately, my reaction upon finishing wasn’t quite on par with the others . . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489508458ra/22221826.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>From the three books I’ve now read, Moriarty seems to have developed a nearly trademarked formula when it comes to her storytelling. Something bad happened at a certain time/place and the reader must follow the wibbly wobbly timey wimey until said something bad is revealed. This time around????<br><br><b>
  <i>“This is a story that begins with a barbecue.”</i>
</b><br><br>Over the course of the show and tell which is the plot reveal, we once again find out everything about the characters they might want to keep under wraps. Some of the “a-ha” moments were pretty obvious (Tiffany’s former life, for example) and some I completely missed the mark at first (I initially thought the “proposal” might be of the swinging variety which shows just why books that use dark or pervy sex storylines don’t put me off at all). Unlike the other selections, this one was . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489508458ra/22221827.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The superbadawful that was revealed was, although traumatic, a fairly common occurrence and the characters just weren’t up to snuff compared to Moriarty’s others. Bottom line, while I still managed to keep turning pages I didn’t feel invested at all in any of these people’s lives and when the already used “memory lapse” trope was drug out for a second book, I couldn’t help but feel . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489508458ra/22221828.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>2.5 Stars because it was perfectly mediocre.</span>

<div id="review_1696242482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696242482" />
    <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts"><img alt="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591195447p2/16496589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1696242482?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts">Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29347945-truly-madly-guilty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts?shelf=advance-copy">advance-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696242482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer455810233217506587"><a href='http://amzn.to/2aIZUqs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon US</a> * <a href='http://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/B01C3NCZTA' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon UK</a><br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470917255i/19980360._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I once saw one of my favourite authors state how much she enjoys the writing of Liane Moriarty which peaked my interest considerably and was the driving factor in me reading TRULY, MADLY, GUILTY, my first story by this author. <br/><br/>The suspenseful and mysterious story arc centers around a fateful BBQ and three contrasting couples who each grow in stature as the trajectory of the story develops. The BBQ is a day that rocks their lives and the catalyst for the suspenseful element </span>
  <span id="freeText455810233217506587" style="display:none"><a href="http://amzn.to/2aIZUqs" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> * <a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/B01C3NCZTA" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470917255i/19980360._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I once saw one of my favourite authors state how much she enjoys the writing of Liane Moriarty which peaked my interest considerably and was the driving factor in me reading TRULY, MADLY, GUILTY, my first story by this author. <br><br>The suspenseful and mysterious story arc centers around a fateful BBQ and three contrasting couples who each grow in stature as the trajectory of the story develops. The BBQ is a day that rocks their lives and the catalyst for the suspenseful element and feel of the story. The exploration of split second decisions, themes of guilt, negligence, culpability, responsibility and the human psyche pertaining to how different people deal with guilt, how they resolve it, the way some do not feel it is all absolutely fascinating. <br><br>The style of Liane Moriarty took me a moment to settle into, initially I felt like the story would miss the rush of feeling I seek when reading but the slow burn of the story had my complete attention by two thirds of the way in and the beauty and thought provoking nature of the feelings ultimately shone through. The time frames jump around unexpectedly which caused me on occasion to have to read back a little to ascertain where and with whom I was currently with, making the transitions appear somewhat jarring. However, by 30% I became accustomed to the unusual style of this author finding that I enjoyed the way the writing made me think a little more, adding to the suspenseful nature and I became completely engaged and intuitive to the writing clues that established the time frame. The third person narrative toggles between the present and the past event of the BBQ providing a full all round perspective and visual of each character’s thoughts, feelings and actions ensuring every element of the story is revealed by the end of the novel providing a very satisfying feeling to the reader. <br><br>I found myself falling in love with the writing of this author. The drops of intrigue she intelligently layers, her rich visual descriptions and faultless characterisations showcasing perfect development throughout the story arc. Their individual agenda's and histories are revealed to the reader depicting the complicated relationships of friends, spouses and good people who make mistakes. The interlacing of the past, the present and the individual stories of each character is brilliant. The plot thickened as I deduced certain aspects and tried to work out others, I think many readers will enjoy being able to solve certain aspects of the puzzle, I certainly did. The last 10% of the novel ties everything together brilliantly and secured this story as a five star read for me. A mysterious tale of how the seemingly ordinary lives of three couples are spiked with extra ordinary events showing how split second decisions can have catastrophic results. TRULY, MADLY, DEEPLY is a compelling read that made me think and to me that makes for an incredible reading experience. <br><br>Note: TRULY, MADLY, GUILTY is a STANDALONE story <br>Genre: Thriller &amp; Suspense, Mystery, Women's Fiction<br><br><br>★ Graphic created by me with a free stock photo from Pexels ★<br><br>** Advanced copy provided from the publisher, via NetGalley, for my honest review thoughts **<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="455810233217506587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
