    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1802830115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802830115" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802830115?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=australia">australia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802830115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1754353250045755238"><br/>The book blurb: <blockquote> Six responsible adults. Three cute kids. One small dog. It’s just a normal weekend. What could possibly go wrong?<br/><br/>Sam and Clementine have a wonderful, albeit, busy life: they have two little girls, Sam has just started a new dream job, and Clementine, a cellist, is busy preparing for the audition of a lifetime. If there’s anything they can count on, it’s each other.<br/><br/>Clementine and Erika are each other’s oldest friends. A single look between them can convey an entire conversation. </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1754353250045755238" style="display:none"><br />The book blurb: <blockquote> Six responsible adults. Three cute kids. One small dog. It’s just a normal weekend. What could possibly go wrong?<br /><br />Sam and Clementine have a wonderful, albeit, busy life: they have two little girls, Sam has just started a new dream job, and Clementine, a cellist, is busy preparing for the audition of a lifetime. If there’s anything they can count on, it’s each other.<br /><br />Clementine and Erika are each other’s oldest friends. A single look between them can convey an entire conversation. But theirs is a complicated relationship, so when Erika mentions a last minute invitation to a barbecue with her neighbors, Tiffany and Vid, Clementine and Sam don’t hesitate. Having Tiffany and Vid’s larger than life personalities there will be a welcome respite.<br /><br />Two months later, it won’t stop raining, and Clementine and Sam can’t stop asking themselves the question: What if we hadn’t gone?<br /><br />In Truly Madly Guilty, Liane Moriarty takes on the foundations of our lives: marriage, sex, parenthood, and friendship. She shows how guilt can expose the fault lines in the most seemingly strong relationships, how what we don’t say can be more powerful than what we do, and how sometimes it is the most innocent of moments that can do the greatest harm.</blockquote>I was honorably, and humbly opening Goodreads this morning to write a review for this book and made the mistake to read a few comments on my other reviews first. Not only did the comments fascinate me endlessly, they also enticed me into other book reviews and discussions, where I read heartfelt, amazing life stories thrown in as part of the reviews, and about four hours later I remembered that I actually wanted to write a review, first and foremost! So to everyone adding so much spice and endless color to my day, THANK YOU! THANK YOU! THANK YOU!<br /><br />Back to business. <br />Liane Moriarty was one of the first (new for me) authors I encountered when I joined GR and have since become one of my all-time favorite authors of mysteries. <br /><br />Social realism. Family dramas. Community tales. Modern challenges. It's all in her books and it is so well presented and mystified. <br /><br />Authors such as Liane Moriarty has the ability to take ordinary lives, and shoot it up into literary brilliance. Of course most authors do that, but Liane Moriarty does it like I would have done it, if I ever had her ability of observation and creative writing. The remark, <i>"Don't let the truth interfere with a good story"</i> is so relevant in this instance. She changes the ordinary into the extraordinary and does it brilliantly without trying to harm the truth. <br /><br />This book reminded me of how I enjoyed taking a different view on my own, as well as the people around me's lives. In this book she took three couples in suburbia and threw them together at a barbeque that would change their course in life forever. They came from different social backgrounds and approached life from different angles, based on their experiences. They could have been my neighbors and friends. All of them. I loved them all for who they were and the values they brought to the table. The only one who had my hackles raised was the hoarder mom. Good lordie! No! Not on my radar for friendship! Never. Even good ole curmudgeon Harry had me crying in the end. He was actually the only one in the book who got me rolling out the tissues on a conveyor belt.<br /><br />The issues are real. The emotions around them are true. The people involved - vulnerable and human. The suspense excellent.<br /><br />However, the first ± 250 pages almost had me giving up on the book. It was that boring and tedious. And to be honest, I probably would have preferred a thorough editing out of at least 150 pages all over the book. But since I knew the best was yet to come, I persisted and yes, my time and energy invested in this tale was rewarded. The plot was perhaps too formulaic. Perhaps the author will consider new surprises, new approaches to her next stories. This formula is getting old. There's nothing really earth-shattering about the book. But it is real. Relatable. Goodness packaged as ordinary people. Respect. <br /><br />For the actual book itself, the boring part included and relevant (after all it almost had my good intentions and excitement to read another book of this author go belly-up), it must be three star rated. But for the way it made me feel, five stars. Look at the reaction it got out of me! So, four beautiful and happy stars it is. For now Liane Moriarty remains one of my favorite contemporary storytellers. And that's it!<br /><br />RECOMMENDED.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1754353250045755238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16451885853231057311">Going into this book I had no expectations. I knew that it had been nominated for best fiction of 2016 on Goodreads (which is why I bought it), but I did not know the author and I did not know much about the story. <br/>Having now finished it I'm so thrilled that I stumbled across this novel on Goodreads.   <span id="freeText16451885853231057311" style="display:none">Going into this book I had no expectations. I knew that it had been nominated for best fiction of 2016 on Goodreads (which is why I bought it), but I did not know the author and I did not know much about the story. <br />Having now finished it I'm so thrilled that I stumbled across this novel on Goodreads. Already from the very first pages I could sense that these characters were lively and the descriptions on point. At several points I was amazed at the authors' sense of details and how these details really brought the story to life. When I gradually realized that this was a story revolving around a focal point - a fatal day - I was hooked, and even though we are told the big twist towards the middle I was hooked throughout. <br />This is a story about family, responsibility and guilt and that is all I can really say. It is beautifully written and structured, and it was such a delight to have these characters in my life for a couple of days - characters that I'm most definitely going to miss and reflect back on in the upcoming weeks. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1738496402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1738496402" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1738496402?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172096-barbara?shelf=2016-challenge">2016-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1738496402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6727777161945541002"><br/>Liane Moriarty is a popular best-selling author and her latest book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty' title='Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'>Truly Madly Guilty</a>, garnered a lot of hype and many good reviews. That said, the book was just okay for me.<br/><br/>Set in Sydney, Australia, the story is about an unfortunate incident that occurs during a backyard barbeque. The cookout's hosts are Vid and Tiffany - a rich sociable couple that live in a luxurious home.....<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935531.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>.....with their 10-year-old daughter Dakota. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935532.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The guests include the hosts' next-door neighbors Erika and Oliver and </span>
  <span id="freeText6727777161945541002" style="display:none"><br>Liane Moriarty is a popular best-selling author and her latest book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26247008.Truly_Madly_Guilty" title="Truly Madly Guilty by Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Truly Madly Guilty</a>, garnered a lot of hype and many good reviews. That said, the book was just okay for me.<br><br>Set in Sydney, Australia, the story is about an unfortunate incident that occurs during a backyard barbeque. The cookout's hosts are Vid and Tiffany - a rich sociable couple that live in a luxurious home.....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935531.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>.....with their 10-year-old daughter Dakota. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935532.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The guests include the hosts' next-door neighbors Erika and Oliver and <i>their</i> friends Clementine and Sam......<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935533._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>.....who bring their two little girls Holly (5) and Ruby (2). <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935534.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story skips back and forth in time, depicting events before the barbeque, on the day of the barbeque, and after the barbeque.<br><br>As the story unfolds we learn the backstories of some of the characters. Erika had a difficult shame-filled childhood with her mother Sylvia, a narcissistic and delusional hoarder. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935535.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Feeling bad for Erika, Clementine's mother Pam took the girl under her wing and pushed Clementine to be friends with her - which Clementine resented. <br><br>Erika's husband Oliver also had a dysfunctional childhood, with two alcoholic parents. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935536.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thus Erika and Oliver - both damaged - understand each other and have a quiet successful marriage.<br><br>Clementine, by contrast, had a happy childhood.....aside from being irritated by Erika's constant presence. Clementine had loving parents, a nice home, and musical talent that was nurtured by her family. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935537.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Clementine is now a professional cellist, happily married to public relations honcho Sam. Though Clementine and Sam's lives are somewhat fraught - with two small kids, two careers, and Clementine's constant fretting about auditions - the couple meanders along quite happily.<br><br>Vid is an electrician who resembles 'Tony Soprano' and Tiffany is a successful property developer with an eye-catching sexy figure. Tiffany unashamedly admits she once worked as a pole dancer to make money for school. The couple enjoy throwing parties and Vid loves to cook - so he serves tasty dishes from recipes he finds on the internet. (I got a yen to try some of his dishes....ha ha ha.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596907334i/29935611._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On the day of the barbeque tension arises early because Erika and Oliver make a request of Clementine and Sam that throws the couple off-kilter. So it's not surprising that there's a little too much drinking and hilarity at the cookout, leading to an unfortunate occurrence. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935538.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A good part of the book drops hints about the incident at the barbeque, details the emotions and actions of the characters, and relates consequences after the cookout. I have to say - after the HUGE build-up - I found the 'barbeque incident' rather predictable and mundane, and the consequences overblown and unrealistic.<br><br>That said there are things I like about the story. It has some clever surprises and twists, and some memorable characters and scenes. For example, Sylvia the hoarder (Erika's mom) is sly, phony, funny....and VERY irritating. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596906185ra/29935542.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And social worker Pam (Clementine's mom) is overly self-righteous in her do-gooding, interfering zeal. At one point Pam gives a dinner party speech that made me (and the book's characters) quite uncomfortable. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596905960i/29935540.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These behaviors - though squirm inducing - add interest to the story. On the other hand, 5-year-old Holly is a hoot when she sprinkles her conversation with "air quotes" on random words.<br><br>The first two-thirds of the book held my attention, after which I was slightly bored. And the story's final scenes didn't ring true to me. I would mildly recommend this book to fans of Liane Moriarty but it's not as good as her earlier work (IMO).<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6727777161945541002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1682858367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1682858367" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1682858367?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1682858367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17562069932927118725">Truly, Madly, Guilty by Liane Moriarty is a 2016 Flatiron Books publication. <br/><br/><br/>I waited, what seemed like forever, to get a copy of this book, while everyone else had already gobbled it up. So, although I make it a practice to avoid reading reviews until I have read the book myself, I couldn’t help but notice this one seemed to be a mixed bag, with some giving it high praise, while others expressed disappointment. But, that happens with most books, really, so I remained optimistic and kept my mind</span>
  <span id="freeText17562069932927118725" style="display:none">Truly, Madly, Guilty by Liane Moriarty is a 2016 Flatiron Books publication. <br /><br /><br />I waited, what seemed like forever, to get a copy of this book, while everyone else had already gobbled it up. So, although I make it a practice to avoid reading reviews until I have read the book myself, I couldn’t help but notice this one seemed to be a mixed bag, with some giving it high praise, while others expressed disappointment. But, that happens with most books, really, so I remained optimistic and kept my mind open.<br /><br />Despite my determination to stay upbeat, I can see why the book received a lukewarm reception from some readers. The author uses her trademark formula of suggesting something horrible, or at least life changing, has happened, but withholds all the information surrounding this mysterious event, while we watch the characters affected by this occurrence cope with the fallout. <br /><br />The story is centered around Clementine and Sam, Erika and Oliver, and Vid and Tiffany, who all gather for a spur of the moment neighborhood barbeque. There is tension in the air right from the start, but things escalate when the atmosphere turns a little flirty and reckless. However, something happens at the BBQ that profoundly affects these couples, causing a ripple through long term friendships and marriages. <br /><br />This method of building suspense works, no matter what the circumstances are, at least to some extent. No one wants to put the book down until they know what the bleep happened and why these couples are floundering. My inherent nosiness, always gets the better of me. <br /><br />However, by the halfway mark, I was beginning to lose patience, and the characters started to grate on my nerves. They all seemed moderately shallow, disconnected from one another somehow, right from the start, so the subsequent disconnect didn’t have the desired effect. <br /><br />Once we are allowed in on the big secret, the catastrophic event that caused such a domino effect, it makes much more sense, and so I had to ruminate on the whole situation for a time in order to decide how I felt about it. <br /><br />But, because the reveal is such a huge secret, I am unable to postulate on the actions and reactions the characters displayed. But, there is an underlying message in this story, and if I’m reading it right and picking up the correct implications, I think it’s something we all need to hear, especially in this judgmental world we live in presently. <br /><br /><br /><br />After collecting my thoughts, I realized the usual laugh out loud humor is not prominent in this one, and other than one or two titillating scenes, the dialogue was a little flat, and the characters did not evoke any kind of emotional response from me, until later, once I fully understood the situation. Then I was able to muster up a little sympathy, or at least understanding, for a few of the characters, while others still left me feeling cold, all of which made the book feel overlong, causing me to experience impatience, and frustration, on more than one occasion, which is something you never want a reader to feel. <br /><br /> While the book has its moments of flair and clarity, the momentum was off, and the usual sweaty palm suspense lost its edge, which has me torn on how to rate this one. So, as usual, when I find myself waffling like this, I settle for sitting on the fence, which means this one gets 3 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17562069932927118725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2305360676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305360676" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305360676?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=modern-fiction">modern-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305360676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14606309135025847785">This is the third Liane Moriarty novel I've read in less than a month, and even I'm surprised at how quickly I've become one of her biggest fans.<br/><br/>I'm also a bit disappointed in myself that it took me so long to check out her books. They're delightful works of contemporary fiction! I had made some (totally wrong) assumptions that I wouldn't like the books, that I wouldn't relate to them because I had heard it was a lot of motherhood stuff and I'm not a mom, that modern novels were somehow less val</span>
  <span id="freeText14606309135025847785" style="display:none">This is the third Liane Moriarty novel I've read in less than a month, and even I'm surprised at how quickly I've become one of her biggest fans.<br /><br />I'm also a bit disappointed in myself that it took me so long to check out her books. They're delightful works of contemporary fiction! I had made some (totally wrong) assumptions that I wouldn't like the books, that I wouldn't relate to them because I had heard it was a lot of motherhood stuff and I'm not a mom, that modern novels were somehow less valuable than classic novels.* All baloney. <br /><br />I love the psychology in Moriarty’s books - her character studies are fascinating and complex. Each novel has its own quirks.<br /><br />Another thing I like about Moriarty's writing is how the plots will go in unexpected ways — I have constantly been surprised at how a storyline will zig when I thought it was going to zag — and I love the way she wraps up a story, sometimes giving the reader who makes it to the end a juicy bit of info that ties the whole novel together. <br /><br />I will admit that <i>Truly Madly Guilty</i> did test my patience a bit, because the structure builds up to a dramatic incident at a barbecue, and it takes us half the book to learn what happened that day. But I am so glad I stayed with this book, because there were themes that really resonated with me, and I learned to love these characters, flaws and all. <br /><br />I'll also make a plug for the marvelous audiobook narrator Caroline Lee, who has beautifully performed the three Moriarty books I've read, and I love her work so much I plan to download her other audiobooks just because she's the narrator. <br /><br />Three cheers for Liane Moriarty and Caroline Lee!<br /><br />*Note: This experience gave me some uncomfortable insight into my own reading biases. I hadn’t realized how I had been subconsciously diminishing the works of some contemporary novelists, when the reality is that some of the “classic” authors who I love were writing contemporary novels of their own time! <br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br />"Clementine learned to feel bad about her white middle-class privilege long before it became fashionable."<br /><br />"She quite liked this aspect of her personality, the way her mood could change from melancholy to euphoric because of a breeze or a flavor or a beautiful chord progression. It meant she never had to feel too down about feeling down." <br /><br />"The cycles of dysfunction and mental illness did not have to carry over from generation to generation. You just had to educate yourself."<br /><br />"No one warned you that having children reduced you right down to some smaller, rudimentary, primitive version of yourself, where your talents and your education and your achievements meant nothing."<br /><br />"It was interesting how a marriage instantly became public property as soon as it looked shaky." <br /><br />"You shouldn't only be nice to nice people."<br /><br />"She thought everyone had friends who felt like obligations."<br /><br />"You could jump so much higher when you had somewhere safe to fall."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14606309135025847785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SswDXgUfW9I0aZlvuazxyV47yqU2iirpBI7Yh7Vv92H3Hhg+g+TwnJMMf9B5W8XGgoznS1Blu7IaFHyyZwWVlA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IvInqDOyMqRP0DK/DyFs0QNOSdezMotahyx59WXxtr+fIDzItUmZ6ui11ADP1lje3/lkOdXdGgGZtt3At5vUSg==')})
  }

And no one embodies this spirit more than Elena Richardson, whose guiding principle is playing by the rules.\n\nEnter Mia Warren--an enigmatic artist and single mother--who arrives in this idyllic bubble with her teenaged daughter Pearl, and rents a house from the Richardsons. Soon Mia and Pearl become more than tenants: all four Richardson children are drawn to the mother-daughter pair. But Mia carries with her a mysterious past and a disregard for the status quo that threatens to upend this carefully ordered community.\n\nWhen old family friends of the Richardsons attempt to adopt a Chinese-American baby, a custody battle erupts that dramatically divides the town--and puts Mia and Elena on opposing sides. Suspicious of Mia and her motives, Elena is determined to uncover the secrets in Mia\'s past. But her obsession will come at unexpected and devastating costs.\n\nLittle Fires Everywhere explores the weight of secrets, the nature of art and identity, and the ferocious pull of motherhood--and the danger of believing that following the rules can avert disaster.Named a Best Book of the Year by: People, The Washington Post, Bustle, Esquire, Southern Living, The Daily Beast, GQ, Entertainment Weekly, NPR, Amazon, Barnes &amp; Noble, iBooks, Audible, Goodreads, Library Reads, Book of the Month, Paste, Kirkus Reviews, St. Louis Post-Dispatch, and many more...\n\nPerfect for book clubs!           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7297076443721569496">Liane Moriarty is the Australian author of six internationally best-selling novels, Three Wishes, The Last Anniversary, What Alice Forgot, The Hypnotist's Love Story and the number 1 New York Times bestsellers, The Husband's Secret and Big Little Lies. <br/><br/>Her breakout novel The Husband's Secret sold over three million copies worldwide, was a number 1 UK bestseller, an Amazon Best Book of 2013 and has</span>
  <span id="freeText7297076443721569496" style="display:none">Liane Moriarty is the Australian author of six internationally best-selling novels, Three Wishes, The Last Anniversary, What Alice Forgot, The Hypnotist's Love Story and the number 1 New York Times bestsellers, The Husband's Secret and Big Little Lies. <br /><br />Her breakout novel The Husband's Secret sold over three million copies worldwide, was a number 1 UK bestseller, an Amazon Best Book of 2013 and has been translated into over 40 languages. It spent over a year on the New York Times bestseller list. CBS Films has acquired the film rights. <br /><br />With the launch of Big Little Lies, Liane became the first Australian author to have a novel debut at number one on the New York Times bestseller list. An HBO series based on Big Little Lies is currently in production, starring Nicole Kidman and Reese Witherspoon. <br /><br />Writing as L.M. Moriarty, Liane has also written a children's book series, The Petrifying Problem with Princess Petronella, The Shocking Trouble on the Planet of Shobble and The Wicked War on the Planet of Whimsy. <br /><br />Liane lives in Sydney with her husband, son and daughter. Her new novel, Truly Madly Guilty, will be released in July 2016. <br /></span>
